B006PTL1QM|5.0|Carl Jung (1875-1961) is known today as a respected psychoanalyst. His father was a protestant minister and Carl maintained a deep interest in religion, spirituality, myths, and even superstition throughout his life. He disagreed with the Sigmund Freud's theory (1856-1939) that the underlying human drive is sex. Thus, for example, Freud says that some people are unable to overcome early sexual attractions to their mother or father and he says art can be a sublimation of the sex drive. While Freud insisted on a strictly scientific study of people, Jung felt that psychoanalysts must also delve into improvable imaginative mystical and spiritual matters. One of his theories is archetypes: ideas can be transmitted from one generation to the next. This is well known. However what is not known is that Jung unprofessionally had long-lasting sexual affairs with at least two of his patients for years.<br /><br /> This 2011 film tells part of the story of Jung's affair with Sabina Spielrein. It began in 1905 and lasted for five years. The film is based on the book by the same name by John Kerr. Spielrein was 19 years old and Jung's first patient. She was ten years younger than Jung who was married. Jung at the time was impressed by the treatment method of Sigmund Freud and used it to treat Spielrein successfully.<br /><br />A serious problem with the Freud method is transference: patients develop a strong feeling of love for the doctor. Thus the author calls it a \\"dangerous method.\\" As expected, Spielrein became enamored with Jung, and Jung, who had stopped loving his wife, took advantage of Spielrein sexually. Jung met Freud in 1906 and began a friendly relationship with him until Freud learnt of Jung's misuse of his profession and sexual affair. Freud ended his relations with Jung in 1913.<br /><br /> Sabina Spielrein became a physician and a psychoanalyst, married, had two daughters, and moved to Russia. She is credited with introducing psychoanalysis to Russia. She and her husband were Jewish. Stalin murdered her husband and the Nazis killed her and her two daughters. After Spielrein left for Russia, Jung, a non-Jew, began an affair with another one of his patients who was also Jewish. Freud with whom Adler had disagreements was also Jewish. In view of Jung repeatedly taking unprofessional advantage of Jews and other acts, as well as articles he wrote during the Nazi regime in Germany in which he spoke disparagingly about Jewish psychoanalysis, there are analysts who are convinced that Jung was an anti-Semite.husband were Jewish. 0307956350|3.0|I liked &#34;The Expats.&#34; The initial premise--a former CIA operative/assassin whose husband knows nothing of her past, just as she seems to know relatively little about him--could easily be ludicrous. Pavone's understated style of writing makes this marital unlikelihood almost believable.  I found his characterization good if not exactly terrific. Mostly done through personality insight rather than appearance description, character development is woven into the thread of the story. Some readers will no doubt dislike the spareness--&#34;But what color was her dress? What kind of shoes was she wearing?&#34;--whereas others (myself included) prefer to build their own mental picture without a lot of paint-by-the-numbers details that add nothing to the plot.  &#34;The Expats&#34; isn't a superficial read. Pavone's disjointed and sometimes confusing use of flashbacks/flashforwards makes it necessary to pay attention to chapter headings, time frames, and the use of the word &#34;had&#34;, indicating past tense. He doesn't spoon feed or beat inattentive readers over the head to make sure they get the gist. Rather he allows us to draw our own conclusions--or to miss the point entirely, whichever the case may be.  If you're looking for something lightweight and undemanding of conscious thought, this one probably isn't for you.  Update, 10/29/15: Found this book laying around the house and decided to reread it (which I occasionally do with books I've enjoyed). This time I would lower the rating I gave to 3-1/2 stars. The protagonist, Kate, is written from a man's point of view. Therefore, she tends to be all over the place personality-wise. She has killed people, walked on 9-inch ledges several stories above the ground in order to break into an office, and stripped down for a backstreet gun dealer to show she wasn't wearing a wire. It's clear that she can take care of herself, and she is hard as nails. But then she goes all soft and sappy and uncharacteristically female,reverting to what the author assumes are inherent female attributes. Pavone goes overboard in trying to explain how an assassin can also be a completely normal woman--a wife and mother of two small children. But realistically, women don't change their stripes any more than men do.  The other thing--again, and as others pointed out--is the jumping back and forth between time frames. Even after a second read, when I knew the basic plot, it was confusing. I don't get the point of this sort of writing. There are better, less convoluted ways to handle flashbacks. In this case, most of the story is a flashback, a fact that sometimes gets lost in the overall shuffle. Losing the reader with weird writing techniques isn't the mark of a great read.

B0002LMLSQ|5.0|It's hard as hell to review instrumental albums, but the music of Ludovico Einaudi is so good that decency demands I throw a few roses in his direction. I bought UNA MATTINA on a whim, and it made me an instant fan. It's seldom that I've heard a piece of music which is so evocative - not only emotionally but visually, creating vivid images within my mind. From the opening notes of the eponymous title track, through to its twelve minute climax, I am transported into a mood so atmospheric it almost becomes a place, and let me tell you, that place is one I want to visit often.<br /><br />UNA MATTINA has thirteen tracks which total one hour and nine minutes of total music, and while there are no losers in the bunch, some songs speak to me more than others. \\"Ora\\" has a slightly classical feel, while \\"Resta con me\\" is all romantic melancholy (as is \\"Dolce Droga\\"). \\"A fuoco\\" broods beautifully, summoning up images of a man in a firelit study looking out at snow covered fields in blue twilight (that at any rate is what I see in my head when this song plays). \\"Nuvole bianche\\" is poignent and passionate at once, demonstrating Einaudi's ability to strike several emotional notes at the same time, while the last track, \\"Ancora\\", is a musical journey which unifies all the themes touched on throughout the album.  As is usually the case with Einaudi's work, the moods dealt with on UNA MATTINA are not happy ones, but redolent of brooding, thoughtful, romantic, melancholy, or instrospective states of mind, occasionally ringing out with intensities of sustained emotion. Einaudi occasionally uses a violin or other instrument to add layers or depth to a piece, but in most cases it simply isn't necessary. The man is living proof of what a piano can do with the right fingers at the keys. Granted the music is pretty specific in terms of the emotional notes it is trying to hit, but there's nothing wrong with specificity - many a great singer or musician has made a career out of striking those notes again and again, and Einaudi is truly a master at what he does. For anyone who hasn't yet heard his work, I'd strongly recommend either this album or the equally lovely DIVENIRE. You won't be disappointed.se notes again and again, and Einaudi is truly a master at what he does. For anyone who hasn't yet heard his work, I'd strongly recommend either this album or the equally lovely DIVENIRE. You won't be disappointed.

0307352145|4.0|\\"Spend your free time the way you like, not the way you're supposed to...Cross the street to avoid making aimless chitchat with random acquaintances...Make a deal with yourself that you'll attend a set number of social events in exchange for not feeling guilty when you beg off....\\"<br /><br />As I read these pieces of advice, I resonated with Susan Cain, her interviewees, and their reflections about navigating career, relationships, and childhood as introverts. Quiet was an interesting foray into the inner world of the introvert. The book challenges the premium that our culture puts upon extroversion, dissects theories of personality, and ends with a section that guides introverts through navigating situations more suited to extroverted characteristics, dialoging with extroverts, and raising introverted children.<br />Overall, the book was fascinating. I talked about it enough that I already have a fellow introvert ready for me to hand it over, so she can read it as well. As an introvert, I found the range of topics within the  chapters sometimes frustrating. As an introvert who likes to stop and reflect, it should come as no surprise that there were moments  of frustration because I was just settling into a topic when the chapter would end and an entirely new angle of introversion would be examined. And a few times I felt like Cain was stretching the research just a bit to make her point, but these slips were forgivable.<br /><br />At the same time that the frequently shifting topics was at times tiresome, I have to give Cain credit for not repeating herself like some non-fiction works do. This isn't one of those books that runs on for 150 pages circling around a vapid observation that could have been made in 30 pages. Each chapter brings fresh discoveries. Her hypothesis that our culture has swapped personality for character is thought provoking, and the studies that bring to light the ways in which group work manipulates our perceptions of right and wrong were downright unsettling. Her book is culturally relevant as she hypothesizes the role that extroverted leaders, who remained unchecked by introverted colleagues, played in the recent stock market crash. And any introvert who reads part four of the book, \\"how to love, how to work,\\" is sure to pick up some insight about how to approach career and relationships in with a healthier and more balanced approach.<br /><br />Note: This book was provided by Waterbrook/Multnomah's Blogging for Books program in exchange for my honest review.

B000QCS8TW|4.0|I never considered myself an admirer of the whole Fantasy genre. There was always a fine line I would never cross over. However, I think I have stumbled onto something very special with A Game of Thrones and the whole A Song of Ice and Fire series. I was pleasantly surprised with this work. Never have I read a book where the chapters are separated into individual characters points of view, centered around that one character and their whole environment-it was very refreshing and brilliant of the author.<br /><br />I have found a little patience is asked of the potential reader when first entering the world of the Seven Kingdoms. The separate chapters and introductions of key characters may seem never ending, but with some interest and an open &#34;trusting&#34; mind follow Mr. Martin into his ever growing epic. However, if you find yourself completely lost with keeping which characters are &#34;direwolf&#34;, &#34;lion&#34;, or &#34;stag&#34;--flip to the back of the books and discover complete lists of houses, families, alliances, brief descriptions (believe me it will serve the new reader well to reintroduce themselves after finishing one book and moving onto the next).<br /><br />In A Game of Thrones, I overall adored the plot and was fascinated with the research that paid homage to medieval elements: the weapons, clothing, feudal system, battle scenes, war tactics, geography etc. It all just flowed beautifully where you believed you entered into a realistic world with minute touches of whimsy. On the note of &#34;whimsy&#34;, I am happy, relieved and thankful to report to any interested readers that there were no to a few clich&eacute; fantasy characters/species. A Game of Thrones (as well as the whole series) is full of betrayal, adventure, drama, mystery, and classic revenge. I found myself gasping when thrilling and dismal surprises touched heroes and villains alike. Throughout the novel(s) the evidence of &#34;grey&#34; characters was an unexpected change from the usual light and dark personalities.<br /><br />The reader will also find that Mr. Martin has a talent to capture and bottle the element of foreshadowing (every &#34;symbol&#34; has a meaning that will resurface with a flash and a boom as the reader progresses into the ever growing plot). I must also note that, it has also come to my attention that Mr. Martin has based his brilliant series on actual history or to more specific the Wars of the Roses and possibly even pulls events and pieces from the hardly mentioned ArmagnacBurgundian Civil War- this creates interest, curiosity for many more topics and events to be explored by any potential reader (you will love History again).<br /><br />The only part(s) in this book (and series) that keeps it becoming a solid 5 star rating (for me) are the graphic sex sections and modern vulgar language. At first, I tried to remember history/ancient beliefs, human conditioning from the Medieval stand point and the warped entertainment expectations of today (sadly, sex sells). All of the needless scenes and language all seemed to sum back to something that unfortunately had to be there to push the realism and sell the product. Realism and product marketing aside, I must confess after awhile the graphic scenes and cussing (that seemed to come out of nowhere) started to wear on me and I desperately wished them gone from my vivid imagination. All negative aspects aside, I am very happy I stumbled upon this series and highly recommend for those readers who wish to escape from the stereotype of &#34;fantasy&#34;.<br /><br />reviewed January 2011, review written 2011personalities. Realism and product marketing aside, I must confess after awhile the graphic scenes and cussing (that seemed to come out of nowhere) started to wear on me and I desperately wished them gone from my vivid imagination. All negative aspects aside, I am very happy I stumbled upon this series and highly recommend for those readers who wish to escape from the stereotype of &#34;fantasy&#34;.  reviewed January 2011, review written 2011

B008LZHA3G|1.0|Bob Dylan's greatness lay in the fact that he could write great poetry and put it to great music, and then sing it in a great, idiosyncratic voice.<br /><br />Nowadays, the voice is shot to hell, and sounds as bad on record as it has done live for the past decade or two. In the doldrum years of the 80's, his output was at an all-time low - uninspired music with embarrassing lyrics. With Oh Mercy, he picked the pieces up again, and managed to produce some excellent albums, but for the past 10 years or so, he has been mired completely in old Americana. And it is getting ooooold. \\"Oh God, not *again*!\\" was my first thought on hearing this album. Not only is it getting terribly old, but simply recreating the old Americana sounds is intrinsically old in itself. There is nothing really new or creative in it. The same old chord progressions, the same old rhythm accompaniment. It is time to lose it, Bob! (Together with that *awful* mustache! Pleeease?)<br /><br />A breakdown of my impressions:<br /><br />Duquesne Whistle - Another standard old swing tune. Compared with the rest of the record, actually one of the most inspired ones, with a passable effort by the band. But still - it's just more of the same old, same old. 3/5<br /><br />Soon After Midnight - Laid-back ballad. The slow tempo at least has the advantage of not putting to much stress on Bob's voice, and without the growling it can actually be called singing to some extent. Still, nothing new here. 3/5<br /><br />Narrow Way - Standard R'n'B rocker. Musically, nothing we haven't heard a thousand times before. Passable. 3/5<br /><br />Long And Wasted Years - Less of a song than poetry recited over a musical background. Music that is repetitive and uninspired, to boot. This is about where the album begins to grate. 2/5<br /><br />Pay In Blood - I defy anyone to decipher the first words without looking the lyrics up on the net - that is how bad Bob's voice is nowadays. A steady rocker, but again - nothing we haven't heard a million times before. Speed it up a bit, and it's a carbon copy of Maybe Someday. 3/5<br /><br />Scarlet Town - Another interminable drag. No real melody, just following the chords progressions note for note. Just drags on and on and on... 2/5<br /><br />Early Roman Kings - And yet another R'n'B slow rocker, following the standard A1 formula. Boring. 2/5<br /><br />Tin Angel - The worst of the lot. Not only is it an interminable drag, the music can hardly even be called music. Just the same extremely basic, monotonous lick being repeated over and over and over... Gaaah! Stop it! I'll confess to anything! Just make it stop! 1/5<br /><br />Tempest - This might sound unbelievable, but after the monotony of Tin Angel, Tempest actually feels like a relief. However, the cheesy lyrics destroy everything. A totally pointless 14 minutes of your life drag endlessly by listening to this. 1/5<br /><br />Roll On John - Cheesy tribute to John Lennon. This is the kind of poetry we all wrote in high school, thinking it extremely poignant and moving. \\"Shine your light. You burned so bright.\\" Come oooon! *sigh* 1/5<br /><br />With the earlier albums, I could at least find one or two songs that I actually like listening to (Workingman's Blues, Spirit On the Water...). On this album, there is nothing I will ever return to.<br /><br />There, I said it. Cue flaming in three, two, one...
